INC-SPECT   Monoenergetic 28.8 +/- 0.1 and 60.9 to 61.9 +/- 0.1   O0292  1   12 
            MeV protons, focused on the target in a spot of       O0292  1   13 
            approximately 8 mm diameter, with a walk of +/- 0.4 cmO0292  1   14 
METHOD     (EDE) The secondary particle type was identified with  O0292  1   15 
           (TOF) A combination of delta-E versus E and flight-    O0292  1   16 
            time versus E, which permitted unambiguous identifi-  O0292  1   17 
            cation over the whole reported energy range. The low- O0292  1   18 
            energy cutoffs for the different particles were       O0292  1   19 
           -------------------------------------------------------O0292  1   20 
             61.7 MeV                                             O0292  1   21 
                  Protons         2.8 -  3.4 MeV                  O0292  1   22 
                  Deuterons       2.3 -  2.9 MeV                  O0292  1   23 
                  Tritons         6.2 -  6.6 MeV                  O0292  1   24 
                  Helium-3        6.6 - 13.1 MeV                  O0292  1   25 
                  Alphas          2.8 - 14.5 MeV                  O0292  1   26

                  Protons                1.8 MeV                  O0292  1   28 
                  Deuterons              1.7 MeV                  O0292  1   29 
                  Tritons                6.2 MeV                  O0292  1   30

                  Alphas                 2.5 MeV                  O0292  1   32 
           -------------------------------------------------------O0292  1   33 
DETECTOR   (TELES,SI,GELI) A solid state three-detector           O0292  1   34 
            telescope, with two silicon delta-E detectors and a   O0292  1   35 
            lithium-drifted germanium detector used for total     O0292  1   36 
            energy absorption. The total resolution was           O0292  1   37 
           approximately 180 keV for most of the data.            O0292  1   38 
           For the 61.7 MeV runs,                                 O0292  1   39 
            the telescope was shielded by tantalum or nickel      O0292  1   40 
            collimators, with thicknesses of 0.432 - 0.653 cm and O0292  1   41 
            areas of 0.183 - 0.522 cm2 +/- 1.5 %, placed at       O0292  1   42 
            distances from the target of 45.8 - 46.4 cm +/- 1%.   O0292  1   43 
            At 28.8 MeV the collimator was 0.013 cm thick         O0292  1   44 
            tantalum with an opening of 0.522 cm2 +/- 1.5%,       O0292  1   45 
            placed at a distance of 45.8 cm +/- 1% from the       O0292  1   46 
            target. The collimator had a misalignment at the      O0292  1   47 
            center of the scattering chamber of +/- 0.5 cm. The   O0292  1   48 
            precision of the detector angle was +/- 0.5 degrees.  O0292  1   49 
            The zero angle was determined to +/- 0.5 degrees. The O0292  1   50 
            angular resolution was +/- 1.2 degrees.               O0292  1   51 
SAMPLE     .Three different aluminium targets were used, with the O0292  1   52 
            following thicknesses and nonuniformities,            O0292  1   53 
               Energy          Thickness       Nonuniformity      O0292  1   54

             61.7, 28.8      1.23 +/- 0.012       +/- 1.5         O0292  1   58 
CORRECTION .The data were corrected for                           O0292  1   59 
            1. nuclear reactions in the germanium detector,       O0292  1   60 
            2. dead layer in the path of the scattered particles, O0292  1   61 
            3. multiple scattering of particles in the first two  O0292  1   62 
               detectors, which made them miss the total absorp-  O0292  1   63 
               tion detector,                                     O0292  1   64 
            4. energy loss of the secondary particles in the      O0292  1   65 
               target,                                            O0292  1   66 
            5. collimator misalignment and beam-spot walk, and    O0292  1   67 
            6. collimator edge penetration by the scattered       O0292  1   68 
               particles.                                         O0292  1   69
